  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_5a2cb0ab-56f3-4ae3-add1-4c0e7db342bc'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer17808803865060607421">Vika Andreyeva can summon the snow and turn ash into gold. Nikolai Karimov can see through walls and conjure bridges out of thin air. They are enchanters—the only two in Russia—and with the Ottoman Empire and the Kazakhs threatening, the tsar needs a powerful enchanter by his side.<br/><br/>And so he initiates the Crown’s Game, an ancient duel of magical skill—the greatest test an e</span>
  <span id="freeText17808803865060607421" style="display:none">Vika Andreyeva can summon the snow and turn ash into gold. Nikolai Karimov can see through walls and conjure bridges out of thin air. They are enchanters—the only two in Russia—and with the Ottoman Empire and the Kazakhs threatening, the tsar needs a powerful enchanter by his side.<br /><br />And so he initiates the Crown’s Game, an ancient duel of magical skill—the greatest test an enchanter will ever know. The victor becomes the Imperial Enchanter and the tsar’s most respected adviser. The defeated is sentenced to death.<br /><br />Raised on tiny Ovchinin Island her whole life, Vika is eager for the chance to show off her talent in the grand capital of Saint Petersburg. But can she kill another enchanter—even when his magic calls to her like nothing else ever has?<br /><br />For Nikolai, an orphan, the Crown’s Game is the chance of a lifetime. But his deadly opponent is a force to be reckoned with—beautiful, whip-smart, imaginative—and he can’t stop thinking about her.<br /><br />And when Pasha, Nikolai’s best friend and heir to the throne, also starts to fall for the mysterious enchantress, Nikolai must defeat the girl they both love…or be killed himself.<br /><br />As long-buried secrets emerge, threatening the future of the empire, it becomes dangerously clear—the Crown’s Game is not one to lose.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17808803865060607421" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/636891-damn-it-i-ve-been-searching-everywheeeere">Damn it! I&#39;ve been searching EVERYWHEEEERE for this kind of book and I, of course, have to WAIT for it to be available?!?!?! I&#39;m gonna dieeeeeeeeeeeeee. Anyone have any similar stories or one relating to Russia? I can&#39;t find any that took place during the Russian Revolution or revolved around what happened then. It can be fantasy or not I don&#39;t care I just.....am gonna go cry now.</a>
</div>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>

</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">The only book worth reading about Russia, that is actually correct, is Deathless by Catherynne M Valente. I see a lot of people recommending The Grish<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">The only book worth reading about Russia, that is actually correct, is Deathless by Catherynne M Valente. I see a lot of people recommending The Grisha Trilogy and as a Russian, I'm telling you, it isn't. Most of it is very loose or she changes it too much for it to be truly representative of Russian-ness. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<div id="review_1471417266" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1471417266" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1471417266?book_show_action=true">Dec 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1471417266" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2129972186303331445"><blockquote>
  <i>She was the sun, and he was a mere rock, drawn in by her gravity. He needed to be closer, to feel her magic, to touch . . . her.</i>
</blockquote><br/>Anyone for another boring, fluffy fantasy full of <s>magic and murder</s> instalove, love triangles and ballgowns?<br/><br/>I'm just going to get the ultimate, overarching problem out of the way first - <b>this book is so so boring</b>. To be honest, I didn't expect that. The blurb alludes to the love triangle and romantic elements so I was prepared for googly eyes and some fast-paced thri</span>
  <span id="freeText2129972186303331445" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>She was the sun, and he was a mere rock, drawn in by her gravity. He needed to be closer, to feel her magic, to touch . . . her.</i>
</blockquote><br />Anyone for another boring, fluffy fantasy full of <s>magic and murder</s> instalove, love triangles and ballgowns?<br /><br />I'm just going to get the ultimate, overarching problem out of the way first - <b>this book is so so boring</b>. To be honest, I didn't expect that. The blurb alludes to the love triangle and romantic elements so I was prepared for googly eyes and some fast-paced thrills, but <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26156203.The_Crown_s_Game__The_Crown_s_Game___1_" title="The Crown's Game (The Crown's Game, #1) by Evelyn Skye" rel="nofollow noopener">The Crown's Game</a> simply <b>lacks any tension</b>.<br /><br />In this world - a fantasy version of Tsarist Russia - there can be only one Imperial Enchanter, one person with magical skill to stand by the Tsar's side. Usually, though, it's pretty simple because only one candidate exists. When more than one exists - in this case, Vika and Nikolai - they must duel to the death over several rounds in The Game. Only one can come out alive.<br /><br />Let me tell you why this potentially awesome premise bored me to tears. <br /><br />Well, firstly, <b>they don't even fucking try</b>! From the very moment that they see one another, a crush develops, and they suddenly forget all of their training and every ambition they've ever had. That's the problem with this book. There's no tension. There's no <i>questions</i> being asked. Will they? Won't they? Dammit, they already have! Before The Game even begins!<br /><br />This is how Vika reacts the moment they meet:<br /><blockquote>
  <i>The instant he touched her, his shadow flickered, and his real self flashed through. Vika sucked in a breath.<br />Oh, mercy, he was handsome, all ebony hair and ink-black eyes and a face so precisely chiseled, Vika could almost picture the blade that had created him. And the sparks that danced through his magic! Goose bumps rose where his hand held her, even though there was a glove and a sleeve between them. Everything inside Vika quivered.</i>
</blockquote><br />The love triangle's third member (though there are arguably multiple love triangles in this book) is Pasha, the heir to the royal throne. Let me tell you something about love triangles - I don't always mind them. No, really. If there are two interesting options involved and realistic reasons why the other person would fall for them both, I can get on board with that angst. But here, it is an <b>unnecessary, forced obstacle</b> that should never have been added.<br /><br />Pasha is not a realistic love interest. There can be no doubt that the main ship here is Vika and Nikolai; the love triangle feels thrown in to create some additional drama. To be honest, this book sorely needed some drama and tension, but Pasha could not create it. He did nothing. The central relationship never feels threatened by him. Also, he adds another dose of instalove:<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“You cannot love her. You hardly know her.”<br />“If there were ever a girl a man could fall in love with without knowing, it would be Vika.”</i>
</blockquote><br />Oh, please.<br /><br />Because everything is so instant, so unexplained, it's hard to take anything seriously. How awful it would be to be forced into a fight to the death with the person you love... and yet, I don't buy Nikolai's obsession with Vika's red curls as "love". Their actions never made any sense. Their feelings seemed hardly more than a crush, so it infuriated me and made me roll my eyes when they were flirting and dancing instead of trying to kill one another.<br /><br />The Game's trials and dueling are dampened by this mutual crush. It never feels like a fight to the death. <b>It feels like tame love taps between two lovestruck teenagers</b>. Of course, in the beginning, they don't know how the other one feels, so it would be natural to assume that the other one really <i>is</i> trying to kill them... and, I don't know about you, but if I thought a cute boy was trying to kill me, I'd rip his cute face off. Just sayin'.<br /><br />One more thing. I am not Russian. I know very little about Russian language and culture. Though if I was going to write a Russia-inspired fantasy, I would do some research beyond reading Bardugo's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10194157.Shadow_and_Bone__The_Grisha___1_" title="Shadow and Bone (The Grisha, #1) by Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">Shadow and Bone</a>. Because it now seems to be the thing in YA fantasy novels for the characters to appear to get drunk on kvass. Which is a soft drink, sometimes with a tiny amount of alcohol (so tiny, it is given to children). <br /><br />Granted - before someone points it out - the book never explicitly states that the kvass gets them drunk. But let's imagine this scenario: <i>A father suddenly discovers that is daughter could be on the brink of death. He freaks out and claims desperately "I need that bottle of Pepsi". He pours himself a glass, throws back his head, and downs it in one. It doesn't quite hit the spot, so he does more shots of Pepsi until the bottle is empty.</i> Maybe it's just me, but something tells me someone is confused about the nature of Pepsi...<br /><br />Anyway, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26156203.The_Crown_s_Game__The_Crown_s_Game___1_" title="The Crown's Game (The Crown's Game, #1) by Evelyn Skye" rel="nofollow noopener">The Crown's Game</a> is a very light, fluffy fantasy, lacking in tension. There seems to be very little to read the sequel for. The ending gives away the obvious direction of the next book and the lack of remaining conflict in their relationship suggests a predictable outcome <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Nikolai comes back, they get to be together <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://society6.com/bookgeek/" rel="nofollow noopener">Store</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2129972186303331445" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1205333749" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1205333749" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1205333749?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1205333749" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9267559623969676269"><blockquote>
  <i>For the winner of the game, there would be unimaginable power.<br/>For the defeated, desolate oblivion.<br/>The Crown’s Game was not one to lose.</i>
</blockquote>Awesome. Great. That's an excellent thing to keep in mind. Do. Not. Lose. Except someone forgot to tell the main characters cause nobody seems to give a shit about winning the game the instant their nether regions start tingling in the presence of the opposite sex.<br/><br/>Having a Russian setting and involving magic, one cannot help but compare this to Leigh Bardugo'</span>
  <span id="freeText9267559623969676269" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>For the winner of the game, there would be unimaginable power.<br />For the defeated, desolate oblivion.<br />The Crown’s Game was not one to lose.</i>
</blockquote>Awesome. Great. That's an excellent thing to keep in mind. Do. Not. Lose. Except someone forgot to tell the main characters cause nobody seems to give a shit about winning the game the instant their nether regions start tingling in the presence of the opposite sex.<br /><br />Having a Russian setting and involving magic, one cannot help but compare this to Leigh Bardugo's <i>Shadow and Bone</i> trilogy. For me, there is no comparison. I admit, it was not the greatest series, but it was interesting and it was entertaining despite the angest and despite the painfulness of the love triangle. If you think you can escape the love triangle here, think again, and this book is even worse because it's just so bloody <i>boring</i>.<br /><br />I used to write really long reviews for books, ripping them apart, criticizing everything that is wrong, but it just seems to tiring to do so these days because I seem to have the same fucking criticism for every quasi-high-fantasy that comes out. Every book has the same problems, this book is no exception. Insta-love. Romance over ambition and rationality. A recycled, boring plot. Acceptable but plodding writing. <br /><br />These days, I can't even be fucked to actually hate a book such as this because I'm just so tired of it all.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9267559623969676269" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1646043056" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1646043056" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1646043056?book_show_action=true">May 22, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=did-not-finish">did-not-finish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=insta-love">insta-love</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1646043056" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12458018175960698952"><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26156203.The_Crown_s_Game__The_Crown_s_Game___1_' title='The Crown's Game (The Crown's Game, #1) by Evelyn Skye' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Crown's Game</a> is not worth it. <br/><br/>Do you want a magical book? Something with romance that will make your heart flutter? A world-building that you’ll never want to leave? And characters you’ll come to worship?<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26156203.The_Crown_s_Game__The_Crown_s_Game___1_' title='The Crown's Game (The Crown's Game, #1) by Evelyn Skye' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Crown's Game</a> has none of that.<br/><br/>At first, I was curious about the game. I love the factor of competition that it brings, but here, we only have two players. Now I want to disclaim that I only read sixty percent of the story, so everything I say, I base it on what I read.<br/><br/>So we have two play</span>
  <span id="freeText12458018175960698952" style="display:none"><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26156203.The_Crown_s_Game__The_Crown_s_Game___1_" title="The Crown's Game (The Crown's Game, #1) by Evelyn Skye" rel="nofollow noopener">The Crown's Game</a> is not worth it. <br /><br />Do you want a magical book? Something with romance that will make your heart flutter? A world-building that you’ll never want to leave? And characters you’ll come to worship?<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26156203.The_Crown_s_Game__The_Crown_s_Game___1_" title="The Crown's Game (The Crown's Game, #1) by Evelyn Skye" rel="nofollow noopener">The Crown's Game</a> has none of that.<br /><br />At first, I was curious about the game. I love the factor of competition that it brings, but here, we only have two players. Now I want to disclaim that I only read sixty percent of the story, so everything I say, I base it on what I read.<br /><br />So we have two players. Who both control magic like true masters. No, really, they’re gifted, and that’s the problem. There can’t be two people with so much power. One has to die. It’s as simple as that.<br /><br />One has to kill the other. Every participant has five rounds. But it’s not something people are excited about. No one is watching them kill themselves. They’re just there hunting one another and pulling off magic tricks they think will kill their adversaries. <br /><br />I wanted to take this book seriously, but it was close to impossible to do that. Don’t say it, Lola, don’t you dare say it—it’s stupid. The competition is stupid. Nikolai tries to kill Vika with birds made of stones for his first round and Vika tries to drown him in the water in front of spectators who think it’s a magic trick for their own pleasure.<br /><br />All I wanted to say to them was ‘Come on! You can do better than that! Where’s your passion?’ <br /><br />And then there’s the romance. I’m not going to talk about it too much, because there’s very little to say. For Pasha, it’s insta-love. He sees Vika and he’s already enamoured of her. Sadly, Vika has her insta-love moment with Nikolai. At some point, I thought Nikolai and another girl would fall in love but he, too, begins to fall for her in the middle of the story. <br /><br />So yeah, I smelled a love-triangle. <br /><br />Another thing my eyes and mind and brain were not able to appreciate was the writing. I hated it. Sometimes it tries to be funny; sometimes it tries to be serious, but the worst part is that it doesn’t create any type of atmosphere. I really didn't feel anything reading this, except for a great amount of annoyance and boredom.<br /><br />It’s all action with this author. There’s a lot of showing, but very rarely do the characters show their feelings, and if they do, it’s not a very deep moment. It’s hard to connect with characters who keep so much to themselves. Obviously, it’s fast-paced, since the author doesn’t linger on emotions, but I often wanted to slow things down.<br /><br />I had some quotes prepared to support my points, but I just remembered again that this book’s not worth it, and I really want to dive into a good book, so I think I’m going to do just that now.<br /><br /><a href="http://www.bookdepository.com/?a_aid=lolareviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">BD</a> | <a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12458018175960698952" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1198948280" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1198948280" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1198948280?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=foodie-fiction">foodie-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1198948280" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3397056137968137013"><b>I had a very severe suspicion that I would like this book when the first chapter started off <i>in a bakery.</i>. </b> I MEAN, HELLO?! CAIT BOOK MUCH?! Also, my #1 favourite thing of recently is Russian inspired fantasy. (Yes I am a big fan of the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10194157.Shadow_and_Bone__The_Grisha___1_' title='Shadow and Bone (The Grisha, #1) by Leigh Bardugo' rel='nofollow noopener'>Shadow and Bone</a> series. OF COURSE.) And walloping me in the face with a) magic, b) Russia, c) dual to the deaths, and d) CAKE...this book + I = very happy together, thank you very much.<br/><br/><b>While the story DOES have magic, it also fetl really historical fictiony?</b> (Ple</span>
  <span id="freeText3397056137968137013" style="display:none"><b>I had a very severe suspicion that I would like this book when the first chapter started off <i>in a bakery.</i>. </b> I MEAN, HELLO?! CAIT BOOK MUCH?! Also, my #1 favourite thing of recently is Russian inspired fantasy. (Yes I am a big fan of the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10194157.Shadow_and_Bone__The_Grisha___1_" title="Shadow and Bone (The Grisha, #1) by Leigh Bardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">Shadow and Bone</a> series. OF COURSE.) And walloping me in the face with a) magic, b) Russia, c) dual to the deaths, and d) CAKE...this book + I = very happy together, thank you very much.<br /><br /><b>While the story DOES have magic, it also fetl really historical fictiony?</b> (Please. Fictiony IS a word.) The author's note says she did a TON of research and studied Russia in college and aHHH YOU CAN TELL AND IT PAYS OFF. I loved the detail. There are so many Russian words and descriptions of places and culture and <i>it was grand</i>. It <b>never skimped on details</b> and I think that made the book more REAL.<br /><br /><b>And the characters?</b> Ohhh, let us speak of the characters. Although I have to admit <b>I didn't actually ever connect to them emotionally?</b> I'm not sure why. They were epic but I think they could've used a little more complexity. <br /><b>• Vika:</b> She's an enchanter, a fiery red-haired totally spunky girl. VERY powerful. VERY fierce.<br /><b>• Nikolai:</b> He's the other enchanter, more like the quiet nerd? But he's very intelligent, as opposed to Vika's punch-them-in-the-face thing going on.<br /><b>• Pasha:</b> He's the Tsar's heir, aaand, he kinda doesn't want to be. He sneaks out, gets grubby with the commoners and is fun and quirky and GENERALLY COOL. I LURVE PASHA THE BEST. (FYI his real name is Pavel. Thank goodness because Pasha does sound mildly like a passionfruit vine. Ahem.)<br /><br /><b>So what was the game about?</b> Oh oh, I'm glad you asked. But firstly, full disclosure: IT WASN'T WHAT I THOUGHT IT'D BE. If you say "game" I start thinking of violent things like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2767052.The_Hunger_Games__The_Hunger_Games___1_" title="The Hunger Games (The Hunger Games, #1) by Suzanne Collins" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hunger Games</a>. Nopity no. It was more like "impress the Tsar with your magic skills"...not actually "blast each other's heads off." Which saddened me a bit? <b>I expected the book to be a high-staked blazing game of glory.</b> Whereas in reality it was a slower moving thing and I didn't actually feel panicked/stressed at all.<br /><br />...but despite that I still loved it??!<br /><br />Like it was easy to read, it was <i>fun</i>, it was SO MAGICAL, like they were magicking amazing things and I loved it. AND IT HAD DELICIOUS RUSSIAN FOOD. <br /><br />There <i>is</i> a love triangle, but I didn't find it irritating AT ALL. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I actually don't even think Vika loves either Nikolai or Pasha?? Hahahhhh...ahem. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <b>But I would say the romance is a bit underdeveloped.</b> I didn't find myself shipping anyone? Although I wonder if that'll change in future books.<br /><br /><b>So this was a DEFINITE good Russiany read for me.</b> I think the writing felt a bit "debut-ish" though, which I think will mature in future books. Aaaand, I think the stakes could've been higher and the characters more complex. BUT HEY. DUDES. TAKE A MOMENT TO APPLAUD THE WORLD BUILDING. I so rarely read nicely detailed worlds like this, so I shall screech from the onion shaped Russian rooftops that I approve.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3397056137968137013" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2421336034?book_show_action=true">Jul 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062422590" href="/book/show/30653914-the-crown-s-game">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2421336034" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3107669677743173558">wow, what an enjoyable story! this has been presented as ‘the night circus’ meets ‘imperial russia’ and it totally delivers in that regard. <br/><br/>i am such a fan of russian history, so i think that was the highlight of the book for me. although the history was slightly skewed (as mentioned in the authors notes at the end), the story was so alive with culture. i loved it! as for ‘the night circus’ part, the only thing in common was that both stories focus on two people who find themselves in the middle</span>
  <span id="freeText3107669677743173558" style="display:none">wow, what an enjoyable story! this has been presented as ‘the night circus’ meets ‘imperial russia’ and it totally delivers in that regard. <br /><br />i am such a fan of russian history, so i think that was the highlight of the book for me. although the history was slightly skewed (as mentioned in the authors notes at the end), the story was so alive with culture. i loved it! as for ‘the night circus’ part, the only thing in common was that both stories focus on two people who find themselves in the middle of a competition to prove who is the greatest enchanter/magician. which was really fun! i love ‘the night circus’ with all my heart, so i was relived that i didnt find myself comparing the two books at all. this book had enough character of its own for it to stand up for itself. <br /><br />what i wanted more from was the writing. for being a book centred around magic, the writing felt so heavy and dull. i wanted to be whisked away by enchantments, by light and whimsical words, but the writing wasnt that at all. it didnt keep me from liking the story, but i think it would have been much more enjoyable had the writing style been a bit different. <br /><br />overall, a really good read and i cant wait to dive into the next book! <br /><br /><b>
  <i>4 stars</i>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="3107669677743173558" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1830033056" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1830033056" />
    <a title="elena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51318038-elena"><img alt="elena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605725028p2/51318038.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1830033056?book_show_action=true">Dec 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="elena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="elena" href="/user/show/51318038-elena">elena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1830033056" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8314421922276719990"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>White moon, angel moon.<br/>Blood moon, demon moon.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Even knowing the mixed reviews this book actually has, I wanted to go into this book without caring about them and not bothering to pay attention to them. It was hard, but I managed to do it. The Crown's Game involves magic and magical elements, involves killing one or the other to become an imperial enchanter, and it even has a Russian setting! Sadly, none of that was something I enjoyed. <br/><br/><i>The Crown's Game</i> is known as a fantasy novel, but</span>
  <span id="freeText8314421922276719990" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>White moon, angel moon.<br />Blood moon, demon moon.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Even knowing the mixed reviews this book actually has, I wanted to go into this book without caring about them and not bothering to pay attention to them. It was hard, but I managed to do it. The Crown's Game involves magic and magical elements, involves killing one or the other to become an imperial enchanter, and it even has a Russian setting! Sadly, none of that was something I enjoyed. <br /><br /><i>The Crown's Game</i> is known as a fantasy novel, but in reality, it's just another <b>Cinderella retelling</b> set in a fantasy world. Set to have one one Imperial Enchanter, one enchanter must have the skills and ability to sweat the other in order to become the trusted one by the Tsar. Nikolai and Vika, the only two enchanters out there with magical abilities, must duel with each other by taking turns throwing out their moves to kill the other. Even if they just took one turn, the Tsar could shut the whole game off and pick his enchanter just like that, but with this Tsar, he wants to make sure he chooses the right one. Only one must come alive, leaving the other one dead because it is believed to not be fair to have one enchanted at the Tsar's side while the other enchanter is still out there with his or her magic, probably planning something out. Only Vika or Nikolai will survive, and the choices lays on the Tsar's hands. <br /><br />This wasn't even fantasy, in my opinion. Sure, Nikolai and Vika have magic abilities and are set to kill each other using their power, but the problem is that first, the whole game is cut off without them even realizing because they don't even try to kill the other. Second of all, the two are falling for each other and are worried or letting go of each other without even realizing they both <b>like each other.</b> Third of all, their magic actually <b>fucking sucks.</b> Honestly, I wish Evelyn created a better aspect of the magical world here because all the magic used and described didn't even sound promising in a way it should sound to kill someone and it wasn't the kind of magic that intrigues me. <br /><br />When it comes to fantasy books, I can never connect to characters, but that doesn't mean I don't <b>like</b> them. With The Crown's Game, I didn't like any of them. I wasn't expecting this book to be like any other book, mainly because I never do and prefer not to since I prefer books to be different even with its small similarities, but I wish this one was. It probably would've made the book better in a way and succeeded to actually blow me away. Sadly, there was nothing--not the characters, not the plot, and not be small plot twist that is there. Like I said, I didn't connect with the characters and that's normal, not unusual. I was glad, since I didn't feel bad for what happened. I'm not gonna give out any spoilers, but the small plot twist along with the end was something I didn't feel bad for. It was surprising, but I didn't feel bad. There's a love triangle and there's insta love. As a matter of fact, there's actually a <b>love rhombus,</b> if that's even a thing. <br /><br /><i>Vika has thoughts about Nikolai the moment she sees him, Pasha is in love with Vika the moment he sees her that he even tracks her down to "learn" about her, Nikolai is in love with Vika but keeps denying it and doesn't even tell Pasha because he doesn't want to hurt his best friends feelings, and Renata, a really close friend to Nikolai, is in love with Nikolai that she tries her best to keep him away from Vika.</i> <br /><br />Because of what Vika thinks about Nikolai, Pasha getting in the way, and Nikolai not wanting to tell his best friend the truth, both enchanters forget about the whole game and what they're meant to do that they both fall for each other without admitting their feelings. Of course, Vika knows but Nikolai, he doesn't admit it until after. <br /><br />Because Nikolai and Vika have feelings for each other, Pasha was known to just be another love interest that would fall for the same girl and would only add drama and tension to it all. He tries his best to be with Vika an convince her, but he also knows she likes Nikolai without a doubt. He doesn't try his best to convince her, since everything he tries is made in a creepy way. I mean, think about it, he tracks her down and always asks Vika's friend where she is because he wants to see her so bad. There's a reason behind him not being able to see her without always wanting to, but I'm not gonna talk about that. There can be a ship between them, but we all know the love interest is between Vika and Nikolai. <br /><br /><b>Nikolai was plain ass weak and stubborn.</b> He didn't even tell Pasha the truth until after and his magic just <i>completely sucked</i>. He was also <i>too controlling of Pasha</i>, telling him he can't be in love with Vika only because <i>he was also in love with her.</i> <b>Vika was too much of a show-off and the way she acted around Nikolai was childish of her.</b> Again, with the whole insta-love thing, the way <i>she thought about Nikolai</i> was childish. What she <i>wanted to do</i> was childish. Her whole personality was childish. <i>Wait, what personality?</i> <b>Pasha was too controlling and fucking creepy.</b> It's like he was Vika's <i>personal stalker</i>. He <i>tracked her down</i>. He <i>asked about her</i>. He <i>seeked information</i> again and again. He <i>fell in love with her</i> without knowing who she was and without caring.<br /><br />Even though I knew there would be romance involved, I actually expected this to be one of those stories where <b>love is forbidden</b> or one of those where <b>love cannot happen but the couple try their hardest even when they know it will not work and they will be sentenced to death</b>. Sorry, I like violence. Even with that being said, I wanted one of them to kill the other. I didn't ship anyone; not Nikolai and Vika, not Nikolai and Renata, and not Pasha and Vika. I didn't care what happened to the other and I didn't care who won. Like always, I didn't have predictions and expectations, but I really didn't care who won. It wouldn't have made a difference for me whatsoever and when I read who the winner was, it wasn't a moment where I was glad, it was more of a moment where I rolled my eyes and said "oh" and that was about it. There are some surprising moments where they had me saying "holy shit" but that was only once, and that is why I gave this an extra star. I felt like that other character and her unexpected show up added even more tension to this as I was reading it. Her chapters were quite exciting, in my opinion, although I hated what happened after. I enjoyed what she did and I was glad with what she did because if I'm being honest, she had a reason. Like I said, this is a spoiler free review so I'm not gonna mention her name or who she is or what she did. <br /><br />The whole Crown's Game isn't even there. <b>It's completely blank and invisible because love is in the way between all three children.</b> It really pissed me off how Vika and Nikolai didn't even try their best to kill each other because they both wanted the <i>other to live.</i> Like I said, I wish this was a story where the love wasn't meant to happen or something because of many reasons set in this. Even though I know nothing about Russia and Russian history, I would've made more sense if love was forbidden or not meant to happen between two enchanters. It would've added more drama and action, and I would've enjoyed it all. When someone reads the description, they might think that Nikolai might kill himself or kill the girl he and Pasha love. Well, not saying which one happens, <b>it takes so fucking long!</b> I've never been so eager to finish a book until now. The book was fast-paced and I enjoyed that, but the moments I had been waiting for happened at the very last, when the book was ending, and it all felt slow-paced after. There's very little magic use and like I said, it all sucked. The enchanters, being enchanters and so powerful like they are known to be, <b>are so weak!</b> The way they actually try to kill each other is a shame, each and every move. <br /><br />Nikolai tries killing Vika with stone birds, while she tries drowning him. The problem is, she spares him because she has feelings for him and wouldn't know what she would do if she killed him without <i>getting to know him or even talk to him</i> and his magic failed to kill her not because he tries not to, but because his magic is weak compared to hers. If her magic was so much more powerful, and if Nikolai was afraid of Vika the moment he actually <i>saw her</i>, why wasn't she able to kill him so quickly? <br /><br />This isn't a fun fantasy novel where there is a major plot twist that will leave you wanting more, it isn't s fantasy novel where there is a world building that will change the way you look at this story, and it isn't a fantasy novel where there is magic used everywhere to kill one another. In fact, it's the opposite. There is no world building. There is no major plot twist. There is no cliffhanger that will leave me wanting more. I don't even know if I want to read the second book, especially with that ending. Honestly, what was the point of that? Seriously Evelyn?<br /><br />The Crowns Game isn't worth it. If you want, go ahead and read it and if you like it, if you like the characters and the way they act around each other and the way the magic is used, good for you. I'm not here to stop you, but I'm here to stop myself from reading something like this. In fact, I was surprised I actually made it through and finished this. There wasn't really a time where I wanted to DNF this book, although I wonder why and how that was even possible. The second book is added to my tbr, but I don't even know if I want to read it now.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8314421922276719990" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText4194570515414612572" style="display:none"><br>What a wonderfully magical and whimsical book – don’t be fooled though, it ripped my heart in half. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1483972589i/21667640._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I’m personally offended that I have to wait <b> 6 entire months </b> before the release of the next book. Like um, no my feelings need to be repaired. #Rood<br><br><i> The Crown’s Game </i> is a historical fiction book that fuses magic with Russian history. Vika Andreyeva and Nikolai Karimov the only two enchanters in Russia and with political unrest increasing in neighbouring empires, the tsar needs an enchanted by his side. <br><br>But which of the two will take that title and walk out with their life?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1467076113i/19549106._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book is written in such a poetic manner, although some people (as you might have seen from all the mixed reviews) found it to be dreary or tiresome, I found the writing extremely captivating. <br><br>The world building was described in such a subtle manner, not taking away from the plot but just enough to construct a beautifully enchanting world. <br><br>What really charmed me was the characters, I must say.     <a title="Sana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26402455-sana"><img alt="Sana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560612398p2/26402455.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1633750653?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sana" href="/user/show/26402455-sana">Sana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=shawty-so-bad">shawty-so-bad</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26402455-sana?shelf=v-emotionally-moving">v-emotionally-moving</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1633750653" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1574817760987978079">Wow, talk about going into a book expecting to be bored as fuck and trashing the shit out of it....and then coming out screaming and loving the crap out of it and screaming so much BECAUSE AHAHAHAHA this was great.<br/><br/>So, I've read The Hunger's Game, but never once, did it occur to me, that THIS BOOK, is literally just like that book. Not once did I compare it even though IT IS SIMILAR. There's just something so???? original and captivating about this book and it was so fun!!! It wasn't until afterw</span>
  <span id="freeText1574817760987978079" style="display:none">Wow, talk about going into a book expecting to be bored as fuck and trashing the shit out of it....and then coming out screaming and loving the crap out of it and screaming so much BECAUSE AHAHAHAHA this was great.<br /><br />So, I've read The Hunger's Game, but never once, did it occur to me, that THIS BOOK, is literally just like that book. Not once did I compare it even though IT IS SIMILAR. There's just something so???? original and captivating about this book and it was so fun!!! It wasn't until afterwards I read someone's review that I saw them point out the similarities between both books and then the realization hit me. <br /><br />Honestly, I can see why many people find this book boring and that's because <b>there is no action and nothing exciting in this book.</b> I wouldn't call it slow paced either because I flew through this beauty. And slow paced book never work out for me. <br /><br />Don't go into this book expecting too much badass action or cool magic because you will not get that. I recommend diving straight into this book knowing nothing because I did that and it worked out great. Many of my friends hated this and thought it was boring. I never bothered to check what this book was about and just started reading with my lowest expectations and I WAS SO SURPRISED BY HOW MUCH I LOVED IT!<br /><br />Pasha is literally like Rhy. He reminded me so much of him. They both are heir to the throne. They are charming, flirty, funny, witty and so loveable. AND I KIND OF SHIP HIM WITH VIKA LMAO, IT'S GONNA SINK ISN'T IT????<br /><br />Nikolai is serious, hot, serious, hot, and quiet. Kind of reminds me of Zuko without the anger. <br /><br />Vika is a badass and strong character and I really liked her. <br /><br />The love triangle can choke.<br /><br /><b>Initial reaction:</b><br />WHAT THE HECK SOMEONE THROW THE NEXT BOOK IN MY FACE, I LOVED THIS. WOW. BYE. IM DECEASED.<br /><br />I DONT KNOW IF I SHOULD GIVE THIS 4 OR 5 STARS SO RATING AND REVIEW TO COME.</span>

          </span>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1633750653">

<div id="review_1499212483" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1499212483" />
    <a title="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink"><img alt="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568991289p2/50044222.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1499212483?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" href="/user/show/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink">Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=recommended-fantasy">recommended-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1499212483" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2431335836215956558">I.... I barely know what to say right now... so here goes ~ a mess of words and emotions. Don't worry, this is spoiler free.<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Imagine, and it shall be. There are no limits."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>First of all, the elephant in the room. <b>The plot of this book is nearly IDENTICAL to the Night Circus. Maybe I should rant about that but you know what.. I didn't really care?</b> I love both books so I didn't mind the nostalgia. There are parts I liked more about each of the books- but I just found myself savoring thi</span>
  <span id="freeText2431335836215956558" style="display:none">I.... I barely know what to say right now... so here goes ~ a mess of words and emotions. Don't worry, this is spoiler free.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Imagine, and it shall be. There are no limits."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>First of all, the elephant in the room. <b>The plot of this book is nearly IDENTICAL to the Night Circus. Maybe I should rant about that but you know what.. I didn't really care?</b> I love both books so I didn't mind the nostalgia. There are parts I liked more about each of the books- but I just found myself savoring this book to pieces regardless. Plus, this one is going to be a trilogy - so I see the series spinning off drastically from where the Night Circus ended. <br><br><i>Okay, now that is out of the way... </i><br><br>HOLY WOW. I just need to point out all the reasons I loved this book.<br><br><u>
  <b>The Magic</b>
</u><br><br>Magic Russia will never ever get old. Never. <i>(BRB going to watch Anastasia now...)</i> And not only is the magic system here lush, it is completely unique and imaginative.<br><br><u>
  <b>The Writing + Pacing</b>
</u><br><br>This is is where I see the most complaints. But honestly, I just savored it. I'm glad it wasn't too fast paced. But yes, this is a slower book... so don't go into it expecting otherwise. The writing itself was every bit as beautiful as The Night Circus - the prose, descriptions.. everything! <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“This was the sort of book one ought to read in pieces, to properly appreciate and savour each bit. And yet he wanted to devour it whole. Messily and all at once.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>I couldn't have said it better myself.<br><br><u>
  <b>The Characters</b>
</u><br><br>I think I can safely say that each character will tug at your heartstrings (though Nikolai was my favorite for obvious reasons.. gentle, sly, and <b>TOPHAT</b>.) Just enjoy discovering each one... I'd rather not give any further hints.<br><br><u>
  <b>The Plot</b>
</u><br><br>As it was in the The Night Circus, the game aspect of the plot was just heartbreaking. It was a bit more vicious in this book... more intense and emotional. Yes, there was a "bit" of insta-love, but it was not handled the way a YA book typically handles it. There was much more of a connection than just attraction even though some things seemed to escalate quickly. I had no complaints in that department. Overall, I was completely swept away in the entirety of this story.<br><br><u>
  <b>THAT ENDING</b>
</u><br><br>Someone help me because I am a WRECK. No, I am not OK. Will I be? That rests in your hands, Evelyn Skye. Please save us all. I literally beg you. PLEASE FOR THE LOVE OF ALL THAT IS GOOD IN THIS WORLD.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464048169ra/19189365.gif" width="280px" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>For real though I need some serious comfort food right now...</span>
  <a data-text-id="2431335836215956558" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1531386918" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1531386918" />
    <a title="Chantal " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31668723-chantal"><img alt="Chantal " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464626501p2/31668723.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1531386918?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chantal " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chantal " href="/user/show/31668723-chantal">Chantal </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=listened-on-audio">listened-on-audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=published-2016">published-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1531386918" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15094344456677040898"><b>Well...for a book about magic <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26156203.The_Crown_s_Game__The_Crown_s_Game___1_' title='The Crown's Game (The Crown's Game, #1) by Evelyn Skye' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Crown's Game</a> was decidedly unmagical.</b><br/><br/>Here on Goodreads I ask people to answer a challenge question when they send me a friend request, the question being: What are some of your biggest bookish pet peeves? The answers are usually pretty similar and include some of the following:<br/><br/>-	Insta-love<br/>-	Love triangles<br/>-	Characters who seem to lose all sense of reason or rational brain function when they meet another character they consider “hot”<br/>-	Lackluster worldbuilding<br/>-	Bor</span>
  <span id="freeText15094344456677040898" style="display:none"><b>Well...for a book about magic <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26156203.The_Crown_s_Game__The_Crown_s_Game___1_" title="The Crown's Game (The Crown's Game, #1) by Evelyn Skye" rel="nofollow noopener">The Crown's Game</a> was decidedly unmagical.</b><br /><br />Here on Goodreads I ask people to answer a challenge question when they send me a friend request, the question being: What are some of your biggest bookish pet peeves? The answers are usually pretty similar and include some of the following:<br /><br />-	Insta-love<br />-	Love triangles<br />-	Characters who seem to lose all sense of reason or rational brain function when they meet another character they consider “hot”<br />-	Lackluster worldbuilding<br />-	Boring plot<br />-	Bad writing and over-the-top metaphors<br /><br />Well my friends, I’m here to tell you that <i>The Crown’s Game</i> contains <b>every single one of these things. It’s been a while since I’ve read such an unoriginal, lackluster and just overall generic book.</b> It’s alright for a book to have tropes, you probably can’t read YA if you’re not ready to handle some of them, but if a story is just made up of <i>all</i> of them, that’s where I draw the line. It made me cringe because it’s practically a “how-to” guide for bad YA and I genuinely cannot understand how an editor was not able to spot this. <br /><br />I've been trying and failing to find something about this book that would be able to redeem it and at least give it something above one star but unfortunately I came up empty. <br /><br />The premise of <i>The Crown’s Game</i> is pretty intriguing. In an Imperial Russia inspired fantasy world, two enchanters are born where only one is allowed to exist. So in order to decide who will become Imperial Enchanter, that is, the magician who will stand beside the tsar and help him rule his kingdom, the two teens – Vika and Nikolai – must duel over several rounds until one of them dies or the tsar chooses a winner. <br /><br />When I first heard this premise I knew I wanted to read this book right away as soon as it was released. The story wasn’t unfamiliar, after all, it’s pretty much <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9361589.The_Night_Circus" title="The Night Circus by Erin Morgenstern" rel="nofollow noopener">The Night Circus</a>, but I figured that in a YA book, set in a Russia-inspired fantasy world it could be amazing. Obviously, <b>this is a classic case of good premise gone wrong.</b> <br /><br />First off, <b>this book is boring.</b> Really boring. How could a magical duel to the death not be exciting, you ask? What could possibly go wrong? Well, for starters, <b>the two enchanters don’t even try.</b> Like seriously, I have rarely seen such undetermined characters. They tell us through their boring inner monologues that they really want to win because reasons, but do they ever show us that? No. From the get-go, they feel a “connection” and the reader immediately knows there won’t be a real game but that instead it will be <b>the story of two hormone-driven teens falling in love (instantaneously). Tension gets thrown out the window the moment the game begins.</b> <br /><br />You don’t believe me? Take a look at Vika’s thoughts, taken from the passage where Vika and Nikolai first meet.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>Oh, mercy, he was handsome, all ebony hair and ink-black eyes and a face so precisely chiseled, Vika could almost picture the blade that had created him. And the sparks that danced through his magic! Goose bumps rose where his hand held her, even though there was a glove and a sleeve between them. Everything inside Vika quivered.</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>Barf. Can you get any more cliché?</b><br /><br />The answer is yes! Enter: love <b>square</b>.<br /><br />So we’ve got insta-love between Vika and Nikolai and we also have insta-love in regards to Pasha who seemingly falls in love with Vika the moment he first sees her. This quote was taken from a passage which happened after Pasha saw Vika for literally two seconds from like 10m away.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>Pasha hooked a leather ottoman with his foot and dragged it closer, then settled deep into his armchair for a long afternoon of reading. But he did not admit it to himself, either aloud or even quietly in his own head, that he was interested in the girl for more than just her magic.</i>
</blockquote><br />Say what?<br /><br />In addition, <b>Pasha was such a flat and archetypical character</b> and it’s pretty clear that the author much preferred Nikolai over him. He was supposed to add drama (which the story desperately needed) but the attempt backfired. Also, can I just say how much I hate when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ friendships break apart because people fall in love with the same person? A person, I might add, they’ve both literally known for a few weeks?!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Throw in a masquerade ball and a gown made of snow and there you have your stale YA fantasy recipe.<br /><br />And how ironic it is that Vika would wear such a gown, because that’s exactly what she is: <b>the most special of all special snowflakes.</b> Since I cannot possibly describe Vika’s beauty, grace, perfection etc. myself, I’ll let Nikolai and Pasha do some of the talking.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>She sparkled like the lanterns under the moonlight<br /><br />“You cannot love her. You hardly know her.”<br />“If there were ever a girl a man could fall in love with without knowing, it would be Vika.”<br /><br />There were few girls he knew in Petersburg society who could traipse through the Savannah without complaining about the burs snagging at their skirts or the dry wind mussing up their hair. But those thoughts didn’t even seem to occur to Vika. <b>She was a mythical creature among ordinary human kind.</b></i>
</blockquote><br />I mean COME ON. The book is FULL of these types of things.<br /><br />The <b>worldbuilding</b> (for which I was super excited) just left me kind of…meh. I’m not going to comment on the depiction of Russia because I really don’t know a whole lot about Russian culture and it’s also an alternate universe so judging the author for historical inaccuracies wouldn’t be entirely fair. What I can say though, is that despite the descriptions of food, this alternate Russia did nothing for me. In terms of <b>magic system</b>, <i>The Crown's Game</i> was disappointing as well. There seemed to be no rules to the magic and the limits that did exist seemed random and convenient. The idea that using magic leaches your energy is not a bad one, just utterly unoriginal and unispired. When one of the central plot points of the story is a magical duel, I expect that an actual magic system is established, as to add cleverness or tension or <i>something</i>. That wasn't the case. <br /><br />Lastly, we have the <b>writing style</b>. Oh boy. I can’t remember the last time I cringed this badly while reading certain paragraphs. I think the author was trying to be poetic and romantic with her weird metaphors but they ended up sounding <b>either incredibly pretentious or were straight out nonsensical</b>. <br /><br />Oh and that ending *rolls eyes*. I'm pretty sure we've all seen it coming from a mile away. <br /><br /><b>Clearly this book did not work for me and I cannot recommend it. If you feel like you can disregard all the tropes and clichés, feel free to give this a try. But if you're searching for a fun and enjoyable YA fantasy, I would steer you elsewhere.</b> </span>
  <a data-text-id="15094344456677040898" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1527369345" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1527369345" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31923026-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533734143p2/31923026.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1527369345?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/31923026-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31923026-laura?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31923026-laura?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31923026-laura?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31923026-laura?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1527369345" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5870681267163188520">The thing that intrigued me most was the impossibility of the situation. One of our main characters would have to die in the end due to the rules of the Crown’s Game. From the start I was fighting to decide who I wanted to root for. And that was before all the additional drama laced in.<br/><br/>The Crown’s Game is the opportunity of a lifetime. It is a competition between enchanters where you demonstrate your magical abilities in an attempt at being chosen as Imperial Enchanter. The Tsar selects the winn</span>
  <span id="freeText5870681267163188520" style="display:none">The thing that intrigued me most was the impossibility of the situation. One of our main characters would have to die in the end due to the rules of the Crown’s Game. From the start I was fighting to decide who I wanted to root for. And that was before all the additional drama laced in.<br /><br />The Crown’s Game is the opportunity of a lifetime. It is a competition between enchanters where you demonstrate your magical abilities in an attempt at being chosen as Imperial Enchanter. The Tsar selects the winner who also becomes his most respected advisor, while the loser gets sentenced to death. Like I said…rough situation. Kill or be killed.<br /><br />Vika is sixteen, lives with her loving father, and believes she is the only enchanter in the empire. (There is usually only one due to lack of magic left). She is under the impression that she is just waiting until she turns 18 to go serve the Tsar. In the meantime, training so that she’s the best Imperial Enchanter she can be.<br /><br />Nikolai is an eighteen year old orphan who was taken in at a young age by cruel Countess Galina in order to train him to use his magic for the future Crown’s Game. Unlike Vika, he’s always been aware he would have an opponent for the Imperial Enchanter title.<br /><br />Pasha is prince, future heir to the throne, and also happens to be Nikolai’s best friend. He cares way more about hanging with his friends than becoming Tsar. He is doesn’t know about Nikolai’s abilities. (or magic in general). And finds himself falling for the new arrival in town, a peculiar girl with seemingly magical abilities.<br /><br />The story is atmospheric with deep world-building and strong characters. I actually can’t rave enough about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/13467894.Evelyn_Skye" title="Evelyn Skye" rel="nofollow noopener"> Evelyn Skye</a>’s world-building. Set in 1825 in Russia, it is clear that she did her research, while also taking an imaginative approach. The setting is detailed and written so beautifully. The characters charmed their way into my heart. There are multiple POVs, even with additional secondary characters that I also couldn’t get enough of. I hope there’s more of them in the second book.<br /><br />The love triangle thing was meh. It was annoying by merely existing, but less of an issue than I thought it would be. However, the insta-love kind of threw me off where that came into play. Dumb. I was hoping for a darker competition or at least one that was more deadly..less “let’s paint the city” more of this:<br /><br /><i>And it was the first time it truly sank in that the things she could do were not only fascinating, but also possibly deadly. She shivered at her own potential; if she were honest, a small part of her thrilled at it, too.</i><br /><br />Other than that, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26156203.The_Crown_s_Game__The_Crown_s_Game___1_" title="The Crown's Game (The Crown's Game, #1) by Evelyn Skye" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Crown’s Game</a> was engaging and unpredictable. I enjoyed the thrilling nature of the story. Can’t wait to see what happens in book 2!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5870681267163188520" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
