<div id="review_1240187419" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1240187419" />
    <a title="Katerina  Kondrenko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36306002-katerina-kondrenko"><img alt="Katerina  Kondrenko" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590049412p2/36306002.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1240187419?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina  Kondrenko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina  Kondrenko" href="/user/show/36306002-katerina-kondrenko">Katerina  Kondrenko</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36306002-katerina-kondrenko?shelf=friendship-bromance">friendship-bromance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36306002-katerina-kondrenko?shelf=read-in-english">read-in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36306002-katerina-kondrenko?shelf=genre-fantasy">genre-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36306002-katerina-kondrenko?shelf=01-out-of-10">01-out-of-10</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36306002-katerina-kondrenko?shelf=read-with-an-effort">read-with-an-effort</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36306002-katerina-kondrenko?shelf=pov-3rd-person">pov-3rd-person</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36306002-katerina-kondrenko?shelf=characters-prince-storage">characters-prince-storage</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36306002-katerina-kondrenko?shelf=plot-logic-is-dead">plot-logic-is-dead</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36306002-katerina-kondrenko?shelf=plot-promising-start-but">plot-promising-start-but</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36306002-katerina-kondrenko?shelf=romance-and-plot-are-in-balance">romance-and-plot-are-in-balance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1240187419" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6734078613973493131"><blockquote>
  <b>1 out of 10</b>
</blockquote><br/><b>Ревью в моем блоге/This review on my blog<br/><a href='http://living-a-thousand-lives.blogspot.ru/2016/05/the-crowns-game-by-evelyn-skye.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Living A Thousand Lives</a></b> <i>(please use Chrome/Yandex browser or Android/IOS to see the page; otherwise, spoiler-tags I use to make my post compact may not work)</i><br/><br/><b>Genre</b>: historical fantasy, AU, YA<br/><b>Stuff</b>: Imperial Russia, magic<br/><b>Fail</b>: the story and its filling<br/><b>POV</b>: 3rd-person, multi<br/><b>Love-Geometry</b>: pissed me off<br/><br/><b>Quote-Core</b>: <blockquote>
  <i>
    “There are things more dangerous than a little magic.”
  </i>
</blockquote><br/>Buddy-read with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/comment/show/152335336' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Vera</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1504139116' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nastassja</a>. <br/><br/>This May was cruel to me: bad </span>
  <span id="freeText6734078613973493131" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>1 out of 10</b>
</blockquote><br><b>Ревью в моем блоге/This review on my blog<br><a href="http://living-a-thousand-lives.blogspot.ru/2016/05/the-crowns-game-by-evelyn-skye.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Living A Thousand Lives</a></b> <i>(please use Chrome/Yandex browser or Android/IOS to see the page; otherwise, spoiler-tags I use to make my post compact may not work)</i><br><br><b>Genre</b>: historical fantasy, AU, YA<br><b>Stuff</b>: Imperial Russia, magic<br><b>Fail</b>: the story and its filling<br><b>POV</b>: 3rd-person, multi<br><b>Love-Geometry</b>: pissed me off<br><br><b>Quote-Core</b>: <blockquote>
  <i>
    “There are things more dangerous than a little magic.”
  </i>
</blockquote><br>Buddy-read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/comment/show/152335336" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Vera</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1504139116" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Nastassja</a>. <br><br>This May was cruel to me: bad book after bad book. I'm tired of negative reviews, but have to do it again, 'cause <i>The Crown's Game</i>, which I'd been waiting for months and supported <a href="http://living-a-thousand-lives.blogspot.ru/2016/04/the-tsars-guard-crowns-game-characters.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>, had failed me.<br><br><b>Russian Stuff</b><br><br><i>Evelyn</i> did her (superficial) research, but it didn't help. Wanna know why? 'Cause a banana skin is not a banana itself.<br><br>This story includes real things from Russian history, Russian words, names and traditions, but they aren't always correct and, what's more important, they lack flesh, power and soul. Croissants for breakfast won't make you look French as well as sombrero on top of your head won't allow everyone to mistake you for a Mexican. I'm not saying that we Russians are that complicated, mysterious and unfathomable, but a few books about our history and a touristic trip aren't enough to get the gist.<br><br>People in <i>Skye</i>'s book have nothing to do with Russians, especially with Russians from the Imperial Times. The way they talk, act, love, make decisions and simply live is wrong. Where are manners? Passion? Culture? I mean, theater, ballet, poetry? Where's Pushkin? His exile was over in 1820s. What about bonded peasants? Renata and Ludmila don't look as people without rights.<br><br><i>The Crown's Game</i> is rather a patchwork quilt which is made of random facts and stereotypes.<br><br><b>Look</b>:<br><br>— Until XX century Russia had no such a name as Victoria (Vika), 'cause it wasn't in our church calendar. There was an analogue, though: Veronica (Nika). Also all my Vika-friends cringe when they hear 'Vickochka'. There are other nicknames for Vika, such as Vickulya, Vickusha, Vickunya. 'Vikochka' sounds weird. <br><br>— Once kvas had indeed been an alcoholic drink, but in XIX century its recipe had changed. Since then it's just a tonic and summer-time cooling thing. <i>Evelyn</i> could use mead or home brew instead.<br><br>— <i>Evelyn</i> thinks that true Russians are <i>hiking through birch forests, playing the balalaika, and having an almost religious zeal for buckwheat kasha with mushrooms and fresh butter.</i> Like really? <br><br>— The ball scene was weird to put it nicely. Suchlike events had its order, guests couldn't start dancing without Tsar and Tsarista's (not Tsarina) arriving. Also there was an order for dances (polonaises, then waltz, then...) and dancers (according to the table of ranks). What I saw in The Crown's Game was a modern masquerade-party.<br><br>— There was Zakrevsky. There was Zakrevskaya. And there were Zakrevskys. Why? It had to be Zakrevskiye. The devil in the details. If you want to sound authentic, go to the mat. <br><br>— “Ochen kharasho, spacibo,” Vika said. (c) You either write a line as it has to be pronounced "Ochin' kharasho, spasiba" or you write it grammatically "Ochen' horosho, spasibo". And an apostrophe in the end of a mellow tones is an important thing. This tiny details can change the meaning. <i>Von</i> is <i>get out!</i>, while <i>von'</i> is <i>stench</i>. There are other language fails. “Dobre dehn.” (c) One can say this is an archaic form of <i>Dobryj Den'</i>, but this form is from another epoch. “Myevo zdarovye.” (c) which had to be <i>Moyo zdorov'e</i>. Bolshebnoe Duplo had to be Volshebnoe Duplo. And so on. <br><br>— Pavel Alexandrovich Romanov. Wrong. In set terms, we put out surnames first. Romanov Pavel Alexandrovich. And no one would call him Pasha. He might be Pavlusha for his mother, but that's it. <br><br>There are more, believe me (check <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1640821793" rel="nofollow noopener">this review</a>, for example). I don't know who was consulting <i>Skye</i> about Russia, but Google could do it better.<br><br>Now listen, I might forget about pseudo-Russia with pseudo-Russians and simply enjoy the story, but...<br><br><b>The Idea</b><br><br>Hello, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1206871997" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>The Night Circus</i>
</a>! I have nothing against similar concepts, they add to new books a nostalgic mood. But <i>The Crown's Game</i> stole too many details from the original and thus ruined the joy. For example, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1428245999" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>A Criminal Magic</i>
</a> is about magic duels too, but it has a unique background (as well as a slow pace with a shitty romance, so don't be excited to read it). <i>ACM</i> isn't a masterpiece, but it shows how to work with a borrowed material without plagiarizing it. Moreover, where <i>The Night Circus</i> had a beautiful atmosphere, <i>The Crown's Game</i> stands empty-handed.<br><br><b>The Characters</b><br><br>They are names without stories. Flat, one-dimensional, dull. I thought their <a href="http://living-a-thousand-lives.blogspot.ru/2016/04/the-tsars-guard-crowns-game-characters.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">promo-profiles</a> would be only the tip of the iceberg, but after this read I learned nothing more. In short, Vika has no personality, Pavel has no spine, Nikolai has no balls. If you shuffle these words, nothing would change, 'cause they all lack personalities, spines and balls. As to minor heroes and heroines, they were only tools.<br><br><b>The Game</b><br><br>We have two enchanters and for some reasons we need only one to survive and become the Imperial Defender and Tsar's Adviser. How we would test our candidates? Maybe we'd check their education? Or ask them to do some strategy work? Or try their powers on battlefield? No, we ask them for a show! And they would try to impress us with renovations and colorful fountains, with thunders and islands, with dancing dolls and beautiful gowns of snow. How the fuck that would help at war?<br><br><b>Love and Instalove</b><br><br>Pavel had a glimpse of Vika from afar and fell for her. Vika had a glimpse of Nikolai standing next to him and fell for him. Nikolai had tried to be reasonable and mature but after a few chapters fell for Vika as well. Mind that I'm talking not about curiosity or sympathy or lust, nooo, they all called it 'love'. Oh dear... There were also desire to suck sugar from fingertips, to kiss this and that, and a lot of crazy metaphors.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>
      "And touching Nikolai, even through her gloves and his sleeve, was like being pummeling by stampede of wild horses. No, wild unicorns. Beautiful, wild unicorns."
    </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><div>
  <br>
  <a href="https://2.bp.blogspot.com/-Pfa3FJ9NeDA/V02PT7BQs9I/AAAAAAAAAso/ASuP5Mz-1qsuHII6Q-tX2_I1DviuByGTQCLcB/s1600/tumblr_nb6hsmONvl1tq4of6o1_500.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img height="179" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464707000ra/19267071.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div><br><br><br><b>The Writing and Logic</b><br><br>The book is easy to read, but it's hard to process in places. Vika's faint from weariness lasts more than 15-30 minutes. This is a fucking coma. Aizhana sleeps with a guy on her own accord and then blame him for her loss of virginity and ruined reputation. Vika learns some bad news, grieves for a while, having a date and just theeeen goes to destroy everything in Nikolai's house, as if in a heat. Is she a slowpoke? Nikolai sends stone birds to attack Vika, she calls for the real ones thinking that their lives would be on Nikolai's soul. Bravo.<br><br><b>The Ending</b><br><br>Predictable meh.<br><br><b>Le-Sigh-Part</b><br><br>And that was one of the most anticipated releases of this year. My intuition sucks.<br><br><b>The Crown's Game (Царское состязание):</b><br><blockquote>— <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1240187419" rel="nofollow noopener">The Crown's Game (Царское состязание)</a> #1/2<br>— <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1435118094" rel="nofollow noopener">The Crown's Fate (Царская доля) </a> #2/2</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="6734078613973493131" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1354062017" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1354062017" />
    <a title="Brittany (Brittany&#39;s Book Rambles)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16373718-brittany-brittany-s-book-rambles"><img alt="Brittany (Brittany&#39;s Book Rambles)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487457172p2/16373718.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1354062017?book_show_action=true">Aug 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brittany (Brittany&#39;s Book Rambles)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brittany (Brittany&#39;s Book Rambles)" href="/user/show/16373718-brittany-brittany-s-book-rambles">Brittany (Brittany&#39;s Book Rambles)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16373718-brittany-brittany-s-book-rambles?shelf=badass-female-mc">badass-female-mc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16373718-brittany-brittany-s-book-rambles?shelf=best-of-2016">best-of-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16373718-brittany-brittany-s-book-rambles?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16373718-brittany-brittany-s-book-rambles?shelf=2016-releases">2016-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16373718-brittany-brittany-s-book-rambles?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16373718-brittany-brittany-s-book-rambles?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1354062017" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8078248838705253048">Привет, друзья! I am here to tell you that you are not prepared for the majesty that is <i>The Crown's Game</i>. You need to know that when you look at that cover, you are looking at a FIVE STAR book. There is magic, romance, a complex plot, drool-worthy guys, and Russian prestige. I. LOVE. IT. It's definitely one of the BEST books I've <i>ever</i> read, and I mean—we're talking Leigh Bardugo levels here, people!<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1399916845ra/9609569.gif' width='400' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I'm always nervous when I read a book that is set in Russia because often times, the language is i</span>
  <span id="freeText8078248838705253048" style="display:none">Привет, друзья! I am here to tell you that you are not prepared for the majesty that is <i>The Crown's Game</i>. You need to know that when you look at that cover, you are looking at a FIVE STAR book. There is magic, romance, a complex plot, drool-worthy guys, and Russian prestige. I. LOVE. IT. It's definitely one of the BEST books I've <i>ever</i> read, and I mean—we're talking Leigh Bardugo levels here, people!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1399916845ra/9609569.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm always nervous when I read a book that is set in Russia because often times, the language is incorrect or something isn't depicted properly. However as your Russian representative and a member of the Tsar's Guard, I can assure you that Evelyn Skye has executed the Russian culture, language, and mentality <i>to a T</i>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1390457115ra/8217321.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If you get a manuscript or an ARC, please be advised that Evelyn has added on the "a" at the end of the last names of the female characters in the book, but the change was made after the ARCs were already printed.<br><br>A note about Russian last names:<br>The endings of surnames are a key not only to a person's nationality but also to their gender. Most Russian surnames change their ending in the feminine: usually the letter "-a" is added at the end (Ivanova, Sorokina), or "-sky" changes into "-skaya (Moskovskaya). However, last names ending in "-ich" and "-ko" are gender-neutral, with the female version not changing its form even when the name is declined (names ending in "-ko", which are particularly common in Ukraine, remain unchanged in all cases, irrespective of whether the person is male or female). <a href="http://rbth.com/blogs/2014/05/22/ivanov_ivanenko_ivanovich_the_meaning_of_russian_surnames_36851.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Source</a>.<br><br>Now that our Russian grammar lesson is done for the day, let me get back to telling you how much I love this book. <i>The Crown's Game</i> was everything I wanted it to be and more. The entire time I was reading, I was flipping out over every page—and we're talking actual shrieking, and jumping up and down. Guys, the book love was <i>intense</i>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1384259643ra/6828817.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>The Crown's Game</i> <b>beyond</b> exceeded all of my expectations. Everything from the plot, the writing, the characters, and the magic—oh my god, the magic! I am in LOVE.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381215794ra/4547802.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I was a flailing mess the <i>entire</i> time while reading this book. Not <i>just</i> because it made me swell with Russian pride, but also because it just kept wowing me.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447647676ra/17033147.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The plot is incredibly intricate with really well-developed characters. You get each character's backstory without feeling overwhelmed. Plus, all of them are so lovable that I got incredibly attached to all of them—even the "bad guys." <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1382191360ra/5744308.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I can confidently say that <i>The Crown's Game</i> is one of my favorite books of ALL TIME and all of you <b>need</b> to read it!<br><br>Read my full review of the Uncorrected Manuscript <a href="http://www.bookrambles.com/2015/11/the-crowns-game-by-evelyn-skye.html" rel="nofollow noopener">HERE</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8078248838705253048" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1608910103" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1608910103" />
    <a title="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44137919-mikee-readwithmikee"><img alt="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583262285p2/44137919.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1608910103?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" href="/user/show/44137919-mikee-readwithmikee">Mikee (ReadWithMikee)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1608910103" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6556470896834748593"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>❝I hereby swear my loyalty to the tsar,<br/>And promise to abide by the rules of the Game,<br/>A duel of enchantment, until a winner is declared.<br/>To this and all traditions here before established, I commit myself<br/>As an enchanter in the Crown's Game.❞</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Rating: {★ ★ ★ ½}<br/><br/>Sadly, I wasn't too blown away with The Crown's Game. This book was one of my anticipated releases of May and I even met Evelyn Skye at YallWest! You could not imagine how disappointed I was to have to rate The Crown's Game only thr</span>
  <span id="freeText6556470896834748593" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>❝I hereby swear my loyalty to the tsar,<br />And promise to abide by the rules of the Game,<br />A duel of enchantment, until a winner is declared.<br />To this and all traditions here before established, I commit myself<br />As an enchanter in the Crown's Game.❞</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />Rating: {★ ★ ★ ½}<br /><br />Sadly, I wasn't too blown away with The Crown's Game. This book was one of my anticipated releases of May and I even met Evelyn Skye at YallWest! You could not imagine how disappointed I was to have to rate The Crown's Game only three stars. I was expecting it to be like the Grisha trilogy but instead, it reminded me of The Night Circus by Erin Morgenstern a tad bit TOO MUCH.<br /><br />The Crown's Game was literally The Night Circus set in Russia. The premise and the characters were the exact same: two rival mentors who have been training their protégés since they were young to prepare them for a competition to the death by showcasing their magic and outdoing the other until eventually, only one is left standing.<br /><br />If this was The Night Circus, Nikolai would be Marco and Vika would be Celia. Nikolai is an orphan. Marco is an orphan. Vika is the "daughter" of Sergei (mentor). Celia is the daughter of Prospero (mentor). The hero learns about the heroine's identity even before the competition starts. A side character named Renata (unrequitedly in love with Nikolai and reads tea leaves) was the parallel character of Isobel (unrequitedly in love with Marco and reads tarot cards) from The Night Circus. Both Marco and Celia started off competing each other in the competition, but as the story progressed, they began to collaborate on their magic. Coincidentally, Nikolai and Celia also collaborated on an enchantment together. And so much more! The similarities were uncanny.<br /><br />I can understand one or two similarities but these two books were the same exact story. Just change the venue from Circus to Russia, change a few names and characters, tweak the plot here and there, and you have The Crown's Game.<br /><br />I believe this book would've been so much better if it wasn't so similar to a book that already existed. To be honest, it's hard to think of something new to write about because almost everybody has done it all, but this was just way too similar. Even if it were inspired by The Night Circus, I wished Evelyn didn't stick to the outline so closely. I feel like unless you read The Night Circus, you wouldn't recognize the resemblance but it is one of my favorite books of all time. Unfortunately, The Night Circus is an older book and not many new people to the YA community would have read it so maybe not a lot of people would notice the similarities. But I could recognize the similarities like the back of my hand.<br /><br />Overall, even if I didn't to compare it to The Night Circus, I found The Crown's Game to be fairly slow. Two hundred pages in and I still wasn't intrigued or blown away by anything that was happening. In fact, not much was happening at all. The book significantly became better in the last 50 pages but even then I felt like things were resolved too quickly.<br /><br />It was a good attempt for a debut novel. If I didn't read The Night Circus, my rating probably would've been higher. However, I had a fun time reading The Crown's Game. It was a quick, little read. Don't get me wrong, the world is magnificent, but I was just expecting something else entirely when I read the synopsis. I may not have personally liked it, but I would recommend this book to readers who love magic and magician-esque plots. I'm looking forward to picking up and reading the sequel!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6556470896834748593" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3577144667" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3577144667" />
    <a title="Sofia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/114413220-sofia"><img alt="Sofia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606141536p2/114413220.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3577144667?book_show_action=true">Oct 06, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sofia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sofia" href="/user/show/114413220-sofia">Sofia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">No one. No one at all.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/114413220-sofia?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/114413220-sofia?shelf=mary-sue">mary-sue</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/114413220-sofia?shelf=failed-romance">failed-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/114413220-sofia?shelf=strong-female-protagonist">strong-female-protagonist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/114413220-sofia?shelf=well-that-was-a-cheap-plot">well-that-was-a-cheap-plot</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/114413220-sofia?shelf=your-typical-ya-fantasy">your-typical-ya-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/114413220-sofia?shelf=how-was-this-published">how-was-this-published</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/114413220-sofia?shelf=love-geometry">love-geometry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/114413220-sofia?shelf=low-fantasy">low-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/114413220-sofia?shelf=stock-side-characters">stock-side-characters</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3577144667" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4901975299471746501">Why do I keep torturing myself with bad fantasy books? <br/><br/>*munches popcorn* *plops onto couch* *sips water* <br/><br/>I believe it's rant time. But first, let's play two truths and a lie. <br/><br/>Vika is one of two enchanters in Russia. She's been training with her father for years, hoping to fill the position of the tsar's second-in-command. But little does she know that Nikolai also wants the job. The tsar declares the start of the Crown's Game, a brutal competition where the two enchanters fight to the death, hop</span>
  <span id="freeText4901975299471746501" style="display:none">Why do I keep torturing myself with bad fantasy books? <br /><br />*munches popcorn* *plops onto couch* *sips water* <br /><br />I believe it's rant time. But first, let's play two truths and a lie. <br /><br />Vika is one of two enchanters in Russia. She's been training with her father for years, hoping to fill the position of the tsar's second-in-command. But little does she know that Nikolai also wants the job. The tsar declares the start of the Crown's Game, a brutal competition where the two enchanters fight to the death, hoping to impress the tsar and gain the position. <br /><br />Where's the lie? Have you guessed it? Here's a little hint... <br /><br /><b>BRUTAL COMPETITION? WHAT BRUTAL COMPETITION?</b><br /><br />Each enchanter has five moves, and their goals are to kill the other enchanter and to gain favor with the Russian people. What does Nikolai do? <b>He paints a house. <i>HE PAINTS A HOUSE.</i></b> Vika's up next, and she's no better. She makes a fountain, and everyone's like <i>oooooh, what a nice fountain,</i> and then she tries to drown Nikolai, but obviously that didn't work because ~lurve at furst sight~ and all that mushy whatever. Nikolai, on the other hand, is so immensely glad he doesn't manage to kill Vika because he's INCOMPETENT but I digress. He's happy she isn't dead because there's something about her... that draws him in... is it LOVE??? COULD IT BE FORBIDDEN LOVE?? OH, I REALLY WONDER. Wouldn't that be a shocker. <br /><br />Just when this couldn't get any worse, TWO LOVE TRIANGLES ARE CREATED. There's Nikolai/Vika/Pasha (the tsarevich), and then there's Nikolai/Renata/Vika. I'm not impressed. <br /><br />So not only is there a massive amount of instalove, the magic system is undefined. Vika and Nikolai have magical instructors, and yet they're supposed to be the only ones with magic. <b>The enchanters can basically do whatever they want, because it's ~fantasy.~</b> And yet their five big displays are ridiculous. And they choose the least effective ways of killing each other. Why doesn't Vika just enchant an arrow to fly into Nikolai's heart while he's sleeping or whatever? The world would benefit. <br /><br />Let's not even mention the horrible writing. The dialogue is so cheesy, it almost feels rehearsed. At one point, Vika says to her father: <br /><br /><i>"Oh, Father. You're all gruff beard on the outside, but mush on the inside.</i><br /><br />Excuse me? EXCUSE ME?? I need to scream, be right back - <br /><br />And the worldbuilding is so weak. Same with the imagery. <b>I know more about the shape of Nikolai's jawline than I do the culture of Russia.</b> Ahem. <br /><br />I don't recommend this. Obviously. <br /><br />1.5 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="4901975299471746501" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1734428220" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1734428220" />
    <a title="Dannii Elle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44487975-dannii-elle"><img alt="Dannii Elle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508499419p2/44487975.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1734428220?book_show_action=true">Aug 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dannii Elle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dannii Elle" href="/user/show/44487975-dannii-elle">Dannii Elle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/26232292-the-crown-s-game">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44487975-dannii-elle?shelf=historical-highness">historical-highness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44487975-dannii-elle?shelf=fantastic-fabrications">fantastic-fabrications</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1734428220" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15264941266970680438">So, historical fiction with a fantastical twist might just be my newest obsession! I absolutely loved everything about this; from the historical setting in 19th century Russia, the imaginative magic system, the focus on the royal hierarchy and the plethora of equally lovable character. I already want more from this world!<br/><br/>The Crown's Game begins in Vika's perspective and the reader is immediately immersed into this strange, ancient world. We learn early on of Vika's magical abilities and the fear</span>
  <span id="freeText15264941266970680438" style="display:none">So, historical fiction with a fantastical twist might just be my newest obsession! I absolutely loved everything about this; from the historical setting in 19th century Russia, the imaginative magic system, the focus on the royal hierarchy and the plethora of equally lovable character. I already want more from this world!<br /><br />The Crown's Game begins in Vika's perspective and the reader is immediately immersed into this strange, ancient world. We learn early on of Vika's magical abilities and the fear from the common folk that this evokes. I felt an initial affinity with her that made me immediately align to her plight. That is until we learn of the existence of another enchanter, Nikolai, and despite him being Vika's adversary I was just as drawn to his character as I was with Vika's. Skye exhibits a brilliance for creating flawed and yet lovable characters as each and every person introduced had a side to them that evoked my empathy and endearment.<br /><br />The Crown's Game, that the title refers to, does not begin until nearly a quarter of the way through the text. I love how the world and the magic system was fully set up before beginning the quest that the rest of the text is dedicated to. From then on the novel is awash with displays of magical ingeniousness that has the reader and the Russian townsfolk equally as enthralled!<br /><br />My only negative is that, despite the disaster that awaits the loser of The Crown's Game and that the two opponents are literally in a duel until the death, there isn't much tension displayed. I loved seeing the pair exhibit their skill in imaginative and thrilling ways, but never once did I worry over the outcome of these beloved characters. I don't exactly know why that is: I immensely enjoyed their journey but felt a little distanced from it, perhaps. <br /><br />This is a book of unique brilliance and I can only equate it to being the literary love-child of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13496.A_Game_of_Thrones__A_Song_of_Ice_and_Fire___1_" title="A Game of Thrones (A Song of Ice and Fire, #1) by George R.R. Martin" rel="nofollow noopener">A Game of Thrones</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9361589.The_Night_Circus" title="The Night Circus by Erin Morgenstern" rel="nofollow noopener">The Night Circus</a>. All I know is, I already can't wait until 2017 and the next installment! </span>
  <a data-text-id="15264941266970680438" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2430458446" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2430458446" />
    <a title="Nasom" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/67824881-nasom"><img alt="Nasom" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520213174p2/67824881.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2430458446?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nasom" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nasom" href="/user/show/67824881-nasom">Nasom</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67824881-nasom?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2430458446" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8542060810296285144">Real rating: <b> 3.5 </b><br/><br/>Buddy read with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/62795872-alexander-hamilton' rel='nofollow noopener'>Red King</a><br/><br/><b> What i liked </b><br/>- I really enjoyed the plot. Like I said in one of my updates, it reminded me so much of the night circus. We have two people who have been trained since they were little to become the king’s enchanter. With two enchanters, there has to be a game to determine who would become the winner. They have to play until one of them dies. To win, they have to either impress the King with their abilities or kill the other enchanter. I enjoyed the comp</span>
  <span id="freeText8542060810296285144" style="display:none">Real rating: <b> 3.5 </b><br /><br />Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/62795872-alexander-hamilton" rel="nofollow noopener">Red King</a><br /><br /><b> What i liked </b><br />- I really enjoyed the plot. Like I said in one of my updates, it reminded me so much of the night circus. We have two people who have been trained since they were little to become the king’s enchanter. With two enchanters, there has to be a game to determine who would become the winner. They have to play until one of them dies. To win, they have to either impress the King with their abilities or kill the other enchanter. I enjoyed the competition which wasn’t a battle but more artistic. I enjoyed reading about what the two enchanters made as they were all beautiful things. <br /><br />- This book has multiple POVs which can be good or bad but I liked it in this. Especially since it was kinda evenly distributed instead of it being mostly in one person’s POV. Also, the chapters are really short (71 chapters) so if you don’t like one person, you don’t have to deal with their POV for a long time.<br /><br />- There was a plot twist I didn’t see coming which was impressive because in YA books, it’s easy to guess plot twists especially in the first book of a series. <br /><br /><b> What i didn’t like </b>. <br />- I really did not like the romance at all. In my opinion, I feel people use the term ‘instalove’ loosely. Crushes on people you just met happens a lot in real life so I don’t mind when it happens in books. But in this, there was instalove. It was even acknowledged in the book. Actually, there were two sets of instalove. How do you still feel ‘connected’ to someone and have dreams of you kissing them when they tried killing you? The love just seemed unrealistic to me. Honestly, I didn’t mind it until the second half of the book where romance seemed to be the main focus. Plus that love triangle wasn’t necessary <br /><br />- I guess the end was supposed to be beautiful but I just found it anticlimactic. <br /><br />Overall, this was an interesting read and I was never bored, but I don’t think I would read the next book because I don’t care to continue lol. It should have been a standalone tbh. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8542060810296285144" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1769074161" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1769074161" />
    <a title="Jiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10502567-jiana"><img alt="Jiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1540380229p2/10502567.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1769074161?book_show_action=true">Jan 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jiana" href="/user/show/10502567-jiana">Jiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062560605" href="/book/show/28595084-the-crown-s-game">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1769074161" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12666865951976862409"><b>Update 01/31/2017</b>: I decided to remove a star and change the rating to 4 stars. Been thinking about it and realized that while the book was indeed great, it still didn't feel like a 5 star read for me.<br/><br/>*<br/>*<br/>*<br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote>“Imagine, and it shall be.<br/>There are no limits.⁠⁠⁠⁠”</blockquote>
</i><br/><br/>I have a confession to make. So I have a shelf here on GR named "Not-Interested", and The Crown's Game was under the "Not-Interested" shelf... *gasp* yep. I have sinned in my past life. But then, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/57334157-caitlin' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cait</a> read it and loved it and recommended it </span>
  <span id="freeText12666865951976862409" style="display:none"><b>Update 01/31/2017</b>: I decided to remove a star and change the rating to 4 stars. Been thinking about it and realized that while the book was indeed great, it still didn't feel like a 5 star read for me.<br /><br />*<br />*<br />*<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“Imagine, and it shall be.<br />There are no limits.⁠⁠⁠⁠”</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />I have a confession to make. So I have a shelf here on GR named "Not-Interested", and The Crown's Game was under the "Not-Interested" shelf... *gasp* yep. I have sinned in my past life. But then, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/57334157-caitlin" rel="nofollow noopener">Cait</a> read it and loved it and recommended it to me, so I was like "fine, will try it" AND LOOK WHAT HAPPENED. A 5 STAR BOOK. I have seen the light. Great.<br /><br />The Crown's Game is Evelyn Skye's debut novel and there are a few flaws here and there, which is expected. BUT <u>I DID NOT CARE ONE BIT.</u> This book was magical, SO VERY MAGICAL. The magic, the description, the scenery... everything was just so pretty to imagine! The writing was brilliant. Not too wordy and not boring. Also, apparently some people found this boring? Fortunately for me, the pacing was great! Only reason it took me a week to finish was because of my slump, but when I finally got out of it, I read the last 200 pages in one sitting!<br /><br />Also, the world building was so well-done! I wasn't confused one bit. The enhancements were so cool and interesting, as well. <br /><br />NOOOOOW. THE CHARACTERS. I LOVE THEM, OK. LOVE, LOVE, LOVE! My favorite is my baby <b>Pasha</b>. #ProtectPashaAtAllCosts OKAY THANK YOU.<br /><br />Our female MC, Vika, is amazing. It's always a big plus for me when the heroine in a fantasy novel is cool because I always tend to dislike them. Vika is clever and headstrong and I just love her! Our male MCs are Nikolai and Pasha. Nikolai is so quiet and brave and *sighs*.... so lovely.<br /><br />You know how a book is all fun and games and then suddenly all hell breaks loose? THIS WAS THE CROWN'S GAME. I was just sitting there reading enjoying it AND SUDDENLY EVERYTHING WAS A BIG FAT MESS. Problem after a problem after a problem and I was like "SLOW DOWN MY HEART CAN'T HANDLE THIS!" and then my heart broke. I didn't really cry, just got teary-eyed but my heart broke so bad and I just wanted to throw the book in my trash bin. Yep. <br /><br />This book has so many mixed reviews and I can see some of the problems other readers have with it, but honestly, the plot, writing and the characters were just <i>so good</i> that I just didn't care at all! I definitely recommend it! As a debut novel, I'd say Skye did a wonderful job. GIVE ME THE CROWN'S FATE NOW, PLEASE AND THANK YOU. <br /><br />*<br />*<br /><br />Buddy reading with my wife <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/54010598-kazzexual" rel="nofollow noopener">EM</a> ♥</span>
  <a data-text-id="12666865951976862409" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1192356866" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14224683821312385469"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1454497474ra/17970459.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/><i>
  <b>There are things more dangerous than a little magic</b>
</i><br/><br/>This book was amazing! I wish it didn't have to end. Fans of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9361589.The_Night_Circus' title='The Night Circus by Erin Morgenstern' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Night Circus</a>, this is what we were looking for! <br/><br/>Vika Andreyeva and Nikolai Karimov are two enchanters who were chosen by tsar to participate in the Crown’s Game. I should note that it`s a very rare case when two enchanters are born at the same time. Both enchanters don`t know about each other, until it`s time to fight in the Game. They also don't know much about the competitio</span>
  <span id="freeText14224683821312385469" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1454497474ra/17970459.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><i>
  <b>There are things more dangerous than a little magic</b>
</i><br><br>This book was amazing! I wish it didn't have to end. Fans of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9361589.The_Night_Circus" title="The Night Circus by Erin Morgenstern" rel="nofollow noopener">The Night Circus</a>, this is what we were looking for! <br><br>Vika Andreyeva and Nikolai Karimov are two enchanters who were chosen by tsar to participate in the Crown’s Game. I should note that it`s a very rare case when two enchanters are born at the same time. Both enchanters don`t know about each other, until it`s time to fight in the Game. They also don't know much about the competition, except for one - they have to demonstrate their abilities and prove who is worthy to serve the king. The loser will face death, because two enchanters cannot exist together.<br><br><i>
  <b>The Imperial Enchanter will need all of Russia’s magic, especially since Bolshebnoie Duplo is no longer as potent as it was when the people of our country still adhered to the old ways. The Imperial Enchanter must be the only major conduit of what magic remains. There cannot be any dilution</b>
</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1454508162ra/17973318.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And now Russia is being threatened by the Ottoman Empire. The King will need all his forces in the looming war. It's time to choose the Imperial Enchanter. But no matter how zealously Vika and Nikolai were preparing for competition, they did not expect that they will penetrate with forbidden feelings for each other. However, their lives are at stake, which means that their relationships are not going to happen.<br><br><i>
  <b>Vika packed the clay from the former pitcher in her hands. It hardened into a ceramic cannonball. “I don’t fancy dying.”<br>Her father emptied the bottle of kvass. “Then the only option is, you cannot.”</b>
</i><br><br>I also should say that the prose was great. The author managed to show Russia in all its glory. After reading this book you will want to see firsthand all of the places visited by the protagonists of the novel. Ornate descriptions of the surroundings were skillfully diluted by exciting dialogues that won`t leave anyone indifferent. The story isn`t fast-paced, but it`s by no means boring.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454506714i/17972832.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454506792i/17972867.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>
  <b>“I’d like to be a menace to anyone who dares to trouble Russia.”<br>“You already are a menace.”<br>Vika pecked Sergei on the cheek. “Then make me a bigger one.”</b>
</i><br><br>If you are expecting ferocious magical battles for the right to become the winner of the Crown's Game, then forget about it. No, as it was in The Night Circus, the main task of enchanters is not to kill each other, but to show their capabilities by working for the good of the country. Each of them is given five attempts to show themselves and to surprise the King. St. Petersburg is their battleground. However, at first enchanters didn`t abandon their attempts to kill each other and to end the Game earlier than it was planned to. With each move their creations impress more and more, but their affection for each other grows too. Nevertheless, both have their own reasons for needing to win.<br><br><i>
  <b>And he could not give that up, because studying with her was his ticket to becoming more than a no-name orphan. He could be Imperial Enchanter someday.</b>
</i><br><br>The romance came to my liking. It wasn`t love at first sight. The enchanters were interested in each other, because they had very different types of magic. Vika copes better with natural phenomena, while Nikolai wields artificial mothers. The only thing that bothered me was Pasha. Personally, I`m not a fan of love triangles, but in the end I warmed to this character.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1454507865ra/17973166.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>For a debut novel I think this book was very impressive. There are a lot of twists and turns that were impossible to guess in advance. All characters are strong-willed and well thought-out. Vika became one of my favorite heroines, and Nikolai is in the list of boys-I-want-to-marry.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1454506648ra/17972816.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I recommend this book to all fans of YA fantasy. I hope it will surpass your expectations, like it did in my case. And I also look forward to the sequel BECAUSE YOU CAN`T END A BOOK LIKE THAT!!! Enjoy your reading :)<br><br><i>
  <b> “Good.” After a long pause, the tsar rose from his wooden throne. “Then let the Crown’s Game begin.”</b>
</i><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="14224683821312385469" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1504139116" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1504139116" />
    <a title="Nastassja" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7734134-nastassja"><img alt="Nastassja" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596034018p2/7734134.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1504139116?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nastassja" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nastassja" href="/user/show/7734134-nastassja">Nastassja</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">no one</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=these-two-are-terrible-together">these-two-are-terrible-together</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=love-triangle">love-triangle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=skipping-pages">skipping-pages</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=special-snowflake">special-snowflake</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=will-not-continue-the-series">will-not-continue-the-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=annoys-the-hell-out-of-me">annoys-the-hell-out-of-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=eye-rolling">eye-rolling</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1504139116" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4248883292087916460"><p>I think I should've been alarmed when I first read these words in the beginning of the story:<br/><i><blockquote><...>but he wanted his daughter to grow up <b>truly Russian</b>—hiking through birch forests, playing the balalaika, and having an almost religious zeal for buckwheat kasha with mushrooms and fresh butter.</blockquote></i><br/>So to speak, the Russian aspect is as true in this story as hiking through birch forests, playing the balalaika and so one are true for Russian people, which is to say - it's bullshit. Not even in the 19th cen</p></span>
  <span id="freeText4248883292087916460" style="display:none"><p>I think I should've been alarmed when I first read these words in the beginning of the story:<br><i><blockquote>&lt;...&gt;but he wanted his daughter to grow up <b>truly Russian</b>—hiking through birch forests, playing the balalaika, and having an almost religious zeal for buckwheat kasha with mushrooms and fresh butter.</blockquote></i><br>So to speak, the Russian aspect is as true in this story as hiking through birch forests, playing the balalaika and so one are true for Russian people, which is to say - it's bullshit. Not even in the 19th century those "hobbies" were a thing a true Russian enjoyed. I don't even want to touch other <i>Evelyn's</i> failures concerning Russian culture (and the were enough of those) but for one I can't ignore: <b>Bolshebnoe Duplo</b> ( a magical hollow) I read. Stopped. Read it again and then couldn't stop laughing for 10 minutes. Like seriously? <i>Bolshebnoe Duplo</i>... Letter <i>B</i> in Rissian means letter <i>V</i> in English and the correct form of the word accordingly would be Volshebnoe. Maybe <i>Evelyn</i> decided to give the <i>B</i> letter a free pass to go amok and feel authentically Russian for once, no matter that English speaking people wouldn't understand author's "love for authenticity" and Russian speaking people wouldn't appreciate the gesture of mutilating their language. <br></p><p>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1465852713ra/19408857.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</p><p>The storyline is no better and resembles one big empty <i>duplo</i> (pun intended). I seriously can't fathom how a book about magical tournament set in <i>Imperial Russia</i> in reality turned out not to be about magic tournament set in <i>Imperial Russia</i>.<br></p><p>
  <i>Than what was it about?</i>
  <br>
</p><p> Insta-love and unicorns.<br></p><p>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1465853045ra/19408869.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</p><p>Guy one saw Girl one and fell for her,<br>Guy two saw Girl one and fell for her, <br>Girl one saw Guy one and fell for him, <br>Girl two was already in love with Guy one.<br><br>WTF?!<br></p><p>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465853045i/19408870._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</p><p>I wouldn't be surprised if stupid clichéd romance in YA books is one of the reasons aliens never visit our planet. I mean, who wants to deal with stupid teenage drama in the first place and when it's a drama in square? Nope. <br></p><p>Apart from everyone loving everyone in this book for no reason, the characters are also <b>shallow, fickle creatures with no substance or depth</b>. And they all are so fucking <i>purrfect</i> I wanted to throw up every time perfection was pushed in my face!<br></p><p>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1465853045ra/19408871.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</p><p>Just come on, how many stories about perfect beautiful people who fell in love from the first sight do we need to read and hate, to hint authors it's time to start creating flawed characters with something more to their name than good looks and lusty glances. <br></p><p>I was reading the book. I was rolling my eyes. I finished the book. I forgot it existed. <br></p><p>That is how I can summarize my reading experience. <br></p><p><i>For more detailed information about the book, go read my friends' reviews with whom I was supposed to buddy-read the book but couldn't due to busy time:</i> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1240187419" rel="nofollow noopener">review #1</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1508435645" rel="nofollow noopener">review #2</a><br></p><p><b>FINAL VERDICT:</b> <br></p><p>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465852713i/19408858._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</p></span>
  <a data-text-id="4248883292087916460" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2474952412" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2474952412" />
    <a title="Maggie ☘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40477684-maggie"><img alt="Maggie ☘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591529603p2/40477684.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2474952412?book_show_action=true">Jul 31, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maggie ☘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maggie ☘" href="/user/show/40477684-maggie">Maggie ☘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=intriguing-world-building">intriguing-world-building</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=unpopular-opinions">unpopular-opinions</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=witches-magicians">witches-magicians</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2474952412" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7648408469325760777">Everyone: Fear the deadly trials! They are mercilles and might very well be the end of you!<br/><br/>The Tsar: Whose birthday surprise I fancy more shall win… <br/><br/>The plot: Scary birthday surprise gift competition ensues. The end.<br/><br/>- A short summary<br/><br/><br/>******************<br/><br/>This was nice and all but... Where were the actual deadly trials?? It seems that no one really cared about them. Not even the tsar who was suposed to initiate them...<br/><br/>I enjoyed the magic and setting. The writing and switch of the POVs was nice as wel</span>
  <span id="freeText7648408469325760777" style="display:none">Everyone: Fear the deadly trials! They are mercilles and might very well be the end of you!<br /><br />The Tsar: Whose birthday surprise I fancy more shall win… <br /><br />The plot: Scary birthday surprise gift competition ensues. The end.<br /><br />- A short summary<br /><br /><br />******************<br /><br />This was nice and all but... Where were the actual deadly trials?? It seems that no one really cared about them. Not even the tsar who was suposed to initiate them...<br /><br />I enjoyed the magic and setting. The writing and switch of the POVs was nice as well (though there were some senseless metaphores included). I did like the characters somewhat, but didn't feel connected to them. As well as I felt disconnected from the romance. It was too much to fast and also love square-y (which was completely unecessary). <br /><br /><br /><i>“Her lungs faltered. Even the mere memory of his magic was so strong. And touching Nikolai, even through her gloves and his sleeve, was like being pummeled by a stampede of wild horses. No, wild unicorns. Beautiful, wild unicorns.”</i><br /><br />WHAT<br /><br />SO IT WAS PAINFUL??<br /><br /><br />The characters were ok, if one dimensional and some of them (Pasha and the whole of non magical citizens) tad dense. The only who had some kind of common sense was Pasha's sister, Yuliana. And she was somewhat antagonized through the female MC's POV by the end. <br />I would've liked this book way more if there was less romance and more viciousness and dueling. Higher stakes. While, in the end, the plot focused more on the romance than the competition itself.<br /> <br />But I think it's more of a problem of false advertising than anything else. Both the beginning of the book and many reviews (and probably the publishers as well) promised deadly competition and, eh, that was... anticlimatic. Thankfully I wasn't expecting it from this book after neing previously warned about the direction of the book, but I get why many people would be dissapointed because of it. Sometimes the advertising that is supposed to help and promote book could more likely hurt the it than anything else. Becasue while the 'duels' were's very much exciting, I still kinda liked them for what they were - creative. <br /><br />Overall: creative, beautiful magic and setting, very romance center (beware the love square), engaging writing but decidedly not dark enough (this is no Hunger Games people). Porbably for fans of Shadow and Bone, though not as good.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7648408469325760777" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ZSE2dmSm2ARHkrw08xFmGEyJ82pO4en+sHk7oPQ0aJg4B9S+Vjxpp41GGLfKb9b4VpiebLi/nm+RNo4zQ+6yJg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xc7cKBrAy+Fx0eU7qo9QtKrr5KpbOgLif4Ka0+tEI3KY6D7gKFp6QrsFQbiT8eBUsPqJrK1kdXNezS9AXJ75zA==')})
  }

  <span id="freeText10780543839950433878" style="display:none">Evelyn Skye is the New York Times bestselling author of THE CROWN’S GAME and CIRCLE OF SHADOWS series.<br /><br />She has a B.A. in Russian literature &amp; history from Stanford University and a J.D. from Harvard Law School. Evelyn was once offered a job by the C.I.A., she not-so-secretly wishes she was good enough to be on “World of Dance,” and if you challenge her to a pizza-eating contest, she guarantees she will win. Evelyn lives in the San Francisco Bay Area with her husband, daughter, and a dog who somehow seems to shed more hair than he weighs.</span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('bookCover_27211901').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('bookCover_27211901').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_27211901').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>

</li>
</ul>
